2025-05-14T23:36:47.264021Z â€” assistant

Great questionâ€”and itâ€™s an important one for workflow clarity:

MPC One+ File Compatibility

The MPC can read and play MP3 files, but:

  • MP3s take longer to load because they must be decoded in real time.
  • They do not stretch or time warp cleanly like WAV files do.
  • Audio editing (chop, reverse, pitch shift) is far more stable and accurate with WAV.

Recommendation:

Always convert your stems and track sources to 16-bit or 24-bit WAV (44.1 kHz or 48 kHz) before importing into your MPC.

Hereâ€™s your ideal setup:

/HAWK-FD-01/swordfish.wav        â† Main track (instrumental or full)
+ optional:
/HAWK-FD-01/swordfish_hook.wav  â† Isolated stems
/HAWK-FD-01/swordfish_verse1.wav

MP3s are fine for reference listening or placeholder clips,
but when youâ€™re slicing, mixing, or resampling: WAV is king.

Want me to help you set up a quick drag-and-drop MP3 to WAV conversion station on the Mac later?
